# Michigan Court Abbreviation Catalogue

A comprehensive catalogue of Michigan state and federal court abbreviations, administrative authority codes, case type classification codes, family law procedures, judicial conduct standards, key doctrines, caselaw, critical deadlines, and research resources used throughout Michigan's legal system.

---

## 1. Michigan State Court Abbreviations

Michigan's courts form the "One Court of Justice" system established by the Michigan Constitution of 1963, Article VI.

| Abbreviation | Full Name | Acronym | Tier |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Mich.** | Michigan Supreme Court | MSC | Supreme Court |
| **Mich. App.** | Michigan Court of Appeals | COA | Appellate Court |
| **Cir. Ct.** | Circuit Court | — | Trial Court – General |
| **Dist. Ct.** | District Court | — | Trial Court – Limited |
| **Prob. Ct.** | Probate Court | — | Trial Court – Limited |
| **Mun. Ct.** | Municipal Court | — | Trial Court – Local |
| **JTC** | Judicial Tenure Commission | — | Administrative / Oversight Body |

### Mich. — Michigan Supreme Court (MSC)

The **Michigan Supreme Court** is the highest court in Michigan. It has superintending control over all courts in the state, possesses final appellate jurisdiction, and its opinions are cited using the reporter abbreviation **Mich.**

> *Constitutional Basis:* Mich. Const. 1963, art. VI, § 1

---

### Mich. App. — Michigan Court of Appeals (COA)

The **Michigan Court of Appeals** is the intermediate appellate court. It hears appeals from the circuit courts, the probate courts, and certain administrative agencies. Opinions are cited as **Mich. App.**

> *Constitutional Basis:* Mich. Const. 1963, art. VI, § 1

---

### Cir. Ct. — Circuit Court

The **Circuit Court** is the highest trial court in Michigan, with general original jurisdiction over:
- Civil claims exceeding $25,000
- Felony criminal cases
- Family law matters (divorce, custody, parenting time)
- Appeals from district and probate courts
- Appeals from certain administrative agencies

> *Constitutional Basis:* Mich. Const. 1963, art. VI, § 11

---

### Dist. Ct. — District Court

Often called the **"people's court"**, the District Court is the most frequently used court in Michigan. It handles:
- Civil claims up to $25,000
- Misdemeanor criminal offenses
- Civil infractions (including traffic tickets)
- Landlord-tenant disputes
- Small claims matters

> *Constitutional Basis:* Mich. Const. 1963, art. VI, § 15

---

### Prob. Ct. — Probate Court

The **Probate Court** has exclusive jurisdiction over:
- Administration of decedents' estates
- Trusts
- Mental health proceedings (involuntary hospitalization)
- Guardianships and conservatorships
- Matters involving minors

> *Constitutional Basis:* Mich. Const. 1963, art. VI, § 15

---

### Mun. Ct. — Municipal Court

**Municipal Courts** are retained by a few cities such as Grosse Pointe. These courts predate the district court system (established in 1968) and continue to operate under local authority, handling local ordinance violations and limited civil matters.

> *Note:* Most municipal courts were replaced by the district court system established in 1968.

---

### JTC — Judicial Tenure Commission

The **Judicial Tenure Commission** is an independent body that investigates complaints against judges in Michigan. The JTC has the authority to recommend discipline—including removal from office—to the Michigan Supreme Court.

> *Constitutional Basis:* Mich. Const. 1963, art. VI, § 30

---

## 2. Federal Court Abbreviations

Federal courts located in or whose jurisdiction affects Michigan.

| Abbreviation | Full Name | Tier |
|---|---|---|
| **U.S.** | United States Supreme Court | Federal – Supreme Court |
| **6th Cir.** | U.S. Court of Appeals for the Sixth Circuit | Federal – Circuit Court of Appeals |
| **E.D. Mich.** | U.S. District Court for the Eastern District of Michigan | Federal – District Court |
| **W.D. Mich.** | U.S. District Court for the Western District of Michigan | Federal – District Court |

### U.S. — United States Supreme Court

The **United States Supreme Court** is the highest court in the federal judiciary and the final authority on federal constitutional questions. Its decisions are binding on all courts throughout the United States.

> *Citation Example:* *Marbury v. Madison*, 5 U.S. 137 (1803)

---

### 6th Cir. — U.S. Court of Appeals for the Sixth Circuit

The **Sixth Circuit** is the federal intermediate appellate court covering **Michigan**, Ohio, Kentucky, and Tennessee. Its decisions are binding on all federal district courts within those four states.

> *Location:* Cincinnati, Ohio  
> *Citation Example:* *Smith v. Jones*, 123 F.3d 456 (6th Cir. 2020)

---

### E.D. Mich. — U.S. District Court for the Eastern District of Michigan

The federal trial court for the **eastern portion of Michigan**, including Detroit, Flint, Ann Arbor, Saginaw, and surrounding areas.

> *Primary Courthouse:* Detroit, Michigan  
> *Citation Example:* *Doe v. Roe*, 456 F. Supp. 3d 789 (E.D. Mich. 2021)

---

### W.D. Mich. — U.S. District Court for the Western District of Michigan

The federal trial court for the **western portion of Michigan**, including Grand Rapids, Lansing, Kalamazoo, **Muskegon**, Marquette, and surrounding areas.

> *Primary Courthouse:* Grand Rapids, Michigan  
> *Division Locations:* Grand Rapids, Kalamazoo, Lansing, Marquette  
> *Notable Cities Covered:* Grand Rapids, Kalamazoo, Lansing, Muskegon, Marquette, Traverse City  
> *Citation Example:* *Doe v. Roe*, 789 F. Supp. 3d 123 (W.D. Mich. 2021)

---

## 3. Court Rule & Administrative Authorities

The primary rule sets and administrative bodies governing the Michigan "One Court of Justice" system.

| Abbreviation | Full Name | Scope |
|---|---|---|
| **MCR** | Michigan Court Rules | General procedure in all Michigan courts |
| **MRE** | Michigan Rules of Evidence | Evidentiary standards in all Michigan courts |
| **SCAO** | State Court Administrative Office | Statewide court administration and standardized forms |
| **MRPC** | Michigan Rules of Professional Conduct | Professional ethics for Michigan-licensed attorneys |
| **MCJC** | Michigan Code of Judicial Conduct | Professional ethics for Michigan judges |

### MCR — Michigan Court Rules

The **Michigan Court Rules** are the principal set of procedural rules governing practice and procedure in all Michigan courts. Promulgated by the Michigan Supreme Court, the MCR covers pleadings, motions, discovery, trials, and appeals.

> *Promulgated by:* Michigan Supreme Court  
> *Citation Example:* MCR 2.116 (motion for summary disposition)

---

### MRE — Michigan Rules of Evidence

The **Michigan Rules of Evidence** govern the admissibility of evidence in Michigan courts. Modeled in part on the Federal Rules of Evidence, the MRE controls what evidence may be presented to the trier of fact at trial.

> *Promulgated by:* Michigan Supreme Court  
> *Citation Example:* MRE 803 (hearsay exceptions)

---

### SCAO — State Court Administrative Office

The **State Court Administrative Office** is the administrative arm of the Michigan Supreme Court. It is responsible for:
- Providing administrative support to the Michigan court system
- Collecting and publishing court statistics
- Developing and maintaining standard court forms used statewide

> *Parent Body:* Michigan Supreme Court

---

### MRPC — Michigan Rules of Professional Conduct

The **Michigan Rules of Professional Conduct** are the ethical rules governing attorneys licensed in Michigan. Violations may result in discipline by the Attorney Grievance Commission and the Attorney Discipline Board.

> *Promulgated by:* Michigan Supreme Court  
> *Enforcement:* Attorney Grievance Commission / Attorney Discipline Board  
> *Citation Example:* MRPC 1.7 (conflict of interest)

---

### MCJC — Michigan Code of Judicial Conduct

The **Michigan Code of Judicial Conduct** sets ethical standards governing the conduct of all judges in Michigan, including standards for impartiality, integrity, and the avoidance of impropriety. It is enforced through the Judicial Tenure Commission (JTC).

> *Promulgated by:* Michigan Supreme Court  
> *Enforcement:* Judicial Tenure Commission (JTC)

---

## 4. Case Type Classification Codes

Every Michigan case number ends with a two-letter alpha code indicating the court's jurisdiction and the nature of the case. These codes are assigned by the State Court Administrative Office (SCAO).

---

### Circuit Court (Cir. Ct.)

| Code | Label | Type | Description |
|---|---|---|---|
| **AA** | Administrative Agencies | Appeal | Appeals from decisions of state and local administrative agencies, including licensing boards and regulatory bodies. |
| **AR** | Criminal Appeals | Appeal | Appeals of criminal convictions or sentences from the district court to the circuit court. |
| **AV** | Civil Appeals | Appeal | Appeals of civil judgments from the district court or probate court to the circuit court. |
| **CH** | Housing | Civil | Circuit-level housing matters, including appeals from district court housing cases or circuit-jurisdiction housing issues. |
| **DM** | Divorce with Minor Children | Domestic Relations | Divorce or separate maintenance cases with minor children, requiring custody, parenting time, and child support determinations. |
| **FY** | Felony | Criminal | Criminal cases involving felony-level offenses. Circuit courts have original jurisdiction over all felony proceedings in Michigan. |

---

### District Court (Dist. Ct.)

| Code | Label | Type | Description |
|---|---|---|---|
| **GC** | General Civil | Civil | General civil claims for money damages up to the jurisdictional limit of $25,000. |
| **LT** | Landlord-Tenant | Civil | Summary proceedings for possession of residential or commercial property, including eviction proceedings. |
| **SC** | Small Claims | Civil | Informal proceedings for civil money claims up to $7,000 (or $10,000 for sole proprietors) where attorneys generally may not represent parties. |
| **SM** | Statute Misdemeanor | Criminal | State-law misdemeanor offenses punishable by up to one year in jail. |
| **SI** | Statute Civil Infraction | Civil Infraction | Non-criminal civil infraction violations, including traffic offenses, where no jail time may be imposed. |

---

### Probate Court (Prob. Ct.)

| Code | Label | Type | Description |
|---|---|---|---|
| **DA** | Supervised Estates | Estate | Formal, court-supervised administration of a decedent's estate, requiring court approval of all significant steps from inventory through final distribution. |
| **DE** | Unsupervised Estates | Estate | Independent (unsupervised) administration of a decedent's estate, where the personal representative acts without routine court oversight, subject to a final accounting. |
| **MI** | Mental Illness | Mental Health | Proceedings for the involuntary hospitalization or treatment of individuals with serious mental illness, including petitions for clinical certificates and hospitalization orders. |
| **JA** | Judicial Admission | Mental Health | Voluntary admission proceedings for individuals who consent to mental health treatment under judicial oversight, as distinguished from involuntary commitment. |

---

## 5. Family Law & Fathers' Rights

Michigan family law is governed primarily by the Domestic Relations chapter of the MCL and the Michigan Court Rules, Chapter 3. The Circuit Court's Family Division has exclusive jurisdiction.

---

### Governing Statutes

| Statute | Title | Key Provisions |
|---|---|---|
| **MCL 722.21–722.31** | Child Custody Act of 1970 | Best-interest factors; joint vs. sole custody; modification standards |
| **MCL 722.27** | Modification of Custody | Court shall not modify unless proper cause or change of circumstances shown |
| **MCL 722.27a** | Parenting Time | Child has right to parenting time with each parent; enforcement tools |
| **MCL 722.621–722.638** | Child Protection Law | Mandatory reporting; CPS investigation; court jurisdiction |
| **MCL 552.1–552.45** | Divorce and Separate Maintenance | Grounds; residency; property division; alimony |
| **MCL 552.451–552.459** | Support and Parenting Time Enforcement Act | Contempt; license suspension; income withholding |
| **MCL 722.711–722.730** | Paternity Act | Voluntary acknowledgment; court-ordered testing; legal presumptions |
| **MCL 552.501–552.535** | Friend of the Court Act | FOC duties; grievance procedures; waiver |
| **MCL 600.2950** | PPO — Domestic Relationship | Ex parte issuance; hearing rights; modification |
| **MCL 600.2950a** | PPO — Non-Domestic Stalking | Stalking-based PPO available to any person |
| **MCL 750.81** | Domestic Assault | Criminal; first offense misdemeanor; basis for PPO |
| **MCL 750.411h** | Stalking | Criminal; basis for non-domestic PPO |

---

### Child Custody Standards

Michigan employs two distinct standards depending on the procedural posture.

#### Best-Interest Factors (MCL 722.23)

Courts must consider and explicitly state findings on **all twelve factors**:

| Factor | Description |
|---|---|
| **(a)** | Love, affection, and other emotional ties between parties and child |
| **(b)** | Capacity and disposition to give child love, affection, and guidance |
| **(c)** | Capacity and disposition to provide material needs |
| **(d)** | Length of time child has lived in a stable, satisfactory environment |
| **(e)** | Permanence of family unit |
| **(f)** | Moral fitness of parties |
| **(g)** | Mental and physical health of parties |
| **(h)** | Home, school, and community record of child |
| **(i)** | Child's reasonable preference (if age/maturity appropriate) |
| **(j)** | Willingness of each parent to facilitate relationship with other parent |
| **(k)** | Domestic violence |
| **(l)** | Any other relevant factor |

> *Authority:* MCL 722.23; *Eldred v Ziny*, 246 Mich App 142 (2001)

#### Standard for Modification (MCL 722.27(1)(c))

To modify a custody order, the moving party must first establish:
1. **Proper cause** — a legally sufficient reason, or
2. **Change of circumstances** — a material change since the last order

Only after this threshold is met may the court conduct a best-interest analysis.

> *Authority:* MCL 722.27(1)(c); *Vodvarka v Grasmeyer*, 259 Mich App 499 (2003)

---

### Parenting Time

**MCL 722.27a** establishes that parenting time is the child's right, not simply the parent's right.

Key principles:
- Parenting time shall be granted in a frequency, duration, and type reasonably calculated to promote a strong relationship
- Neither parent may unilaterally deny the other's parenting time
- Makeup time is a remedy for improperly denied parenting time
- The court may impose conditions: drug testing, supervision, exchange procedures

**Enforcement Mechanisms:**
1. Contempt of court (MCR 3.208; MCL 552.641)
2. Show cause / bench warrant
3. Makeup parenting time order
4. Modification of custody as sanction for willful denial
5. FOC enforcement complaint

> *Authority:* MCL 722.27a; *Rivette v Rose-Molina*, 278 Mich App 327 (2008)

---

### Child Support

Michigan uses the **Michigan Child Support Formula (MCSF)**, promulgated by the Michigan Supreme Court and updated periodically. The formula is presumptively correct.

Key components:
- **Base support** — calculated from net incomes of both parents and overnight percentage
- **Medical support** — health insurance and uninsured medical expense sharing
- **Child care support** — work/school-related child care costs
- **Deviation** — court may deviate from MCSF if application would be unjust or inappropriate; *must* state findings

**Income Withholding (IWO):** All Michigan support orders contain an automatic income withholding order unless the court finds good cause to deviate.

**Imputed Income:** If a parent is voluntarily unemployed or underemployed, the court may impute income at the parent's potential earning capacity.

> *Authority:* MCL 552.519; MCL 552.605; MCSF Manual (current edition); *Ghidotti v Barber*, 459 Mich 189 (1998)

---

### Paternity

| Method | Authority | Description |
|---|---|---|
| **Voluntary Acknowledgment of Paternity (VAP)** | MCL 722.1003 | Signed at hospital or later; has same effect as court order; can be rescinded within 60 days |
| **Presumed Father** | MCL 722.711(a) | Man married to mother at time of child's birth |
| **Court-Ordered Genetic Testing** | MCL 722.716 | Testing may be ordered in paternity proceedings; results >99% create rebuttable presumption |
| **Affidavit of Parentage** | MCL 722.1003 | Same as VAP; filed with SCAO vital records |
| **Order of Filiation** | MCL 722.717 | Court order establishing legal paternity; triggers custody/support rights |

**Key Rights Upon Establishing Paternity:**
- Right to seek custody or parenting time
- Obligation for child support
- Inheritance rights for child
- Right to notice in adoption proceedings

> *Authority:* Paternity Act, MCL 722.711 et seq.; *In re KH*, 469 Mich 621 (2004)

---

### Personal Protection Orders (PPO)

See detailed PPO Defense Toolkit in §12 below.

**Summary:**

| Type | Authority | Basis |
|---|---|---|
| Domestic Relationship PPO | MCL 600.2950 | Assault, threatening behavior, stalking by intimate partner/family member |
| Non-Domestic Stalking PPO | MCL 600.2950a | Stalking by any person regardless of relationship |

Ex parte PPOs are issued without notice; respondent must file a motion to modify or terminate within **14 days** of service (MCR 3.703(G)).

---

### Joint vs. Sole Custody — Legal & Physical Distinctions

**Legal Custody** — decision-making authority over major life decisions (education, medical, religion):

| Type | Description | Standard |
|---|---|---|
| **Sole legal custody** | One parent has final decision-making authority | Awarded when joint legal custody is not in the best interests of the child |
| **Joint legal custody** | Both parents share major decisions | Presumptively preferred; requires that parents can cooperate; *Bofysil v Bofysil*, 239 Mich App 667 (2000) |

**Physical Custody** — where the child primarily resides:

| Type | Description |
|---|---|
| **Sole physical custody** | Child resides primarily with one parent; other has parenting time |
| **Joint physical custody** | Child spends substantial time with both parents; often defined by overnights for MCSF purposes |

> *Authority:* MCL 722.26a (joint custody statute); MCL 722.26b (joint custody granted on request unless not in best interests); *Bofysil v Bofysil*, 239 Mich App 667 (2000); *Pierron v Pierron*, 486 Mich 81 (2010)

**Joint Custody — Required Findings (MCL 722.26a(1)):**
Before awarding joint custody, the court must consider:
1. The agreement or lack thereof of the parents
2. Whether the parents will be able to cooperate and generally agree concerning important decisions affecting the welfare of the child
3. Whether domestic violence is present
4. Geographical separation of parents
5. Established custodial environment

---

### Emergency Ex Parte Custody Orders (EPOC)

A parent may request an emergency ex parte custody order when immediate action is necessary to protect the child.

**Standards for EPOC (MCR 3.207(B); MCL 722.27c):**
1. Irreparable harm will result if the ex parte order is not issued
2. The harm is immediate — no time to provide notice
3. Supporting affidavit with specific facts (not conclusory)

**Procedure:**
1. File verified motion and affidavit with circuit court family division (CC 385 or similar)
2. Clerk presents to duty judge immediately
3. Judge rules same day (ex parte — no notice to opposing party)
4. Order served on other parent with a return hearing date (within 14 days, MCR 3.207(B)(3))
5. At return hearing, regular temporary order standards apply; opposing party may contest

> *Note:* Courts disfavor EPOC without genuine emergency; filing an unwarranted EPOC may harm the requesting party in the best-interest analysis (factor (j) — facilitating the other parent's relationship).

---

### Guardian Ad Litem (GAL) Appointment

Courts may appoint a **Guardian Ad Litem** (GAL) or **Children's Lawyer** to represent the interests of a minor child in contested custody proceedings.

| Role | Authority | Purpose |
|---|---|---|
| **Guardian ad litem** | MCL 722.24; MCR 5.121 | Investigates child's best interests; reports to court; may testify |
| **Children's attorney** | MCR 3.916 | Acts as traditional attorney for child; represents child's stated wishes |
| **CASA volunteer** | MCL 722.632 | Court Appointed Special Advocate; lay volunteer who monitors child's welfare |

**When Appointed:**
- High-conflict custody cases
- Allegations of abuse or neglect in custody context
- Child's preference is a significant disputed issue
- Drug or alcohol abuse allegations

**Costs:** Courts may allocate GAL fees between parties (MCL 722.24(2)); may be waived if parties are indigent.

---

### MCSF Child Support Calculation — Step-by-Step

The **Michigan Child Support Formula (MCSF)** calculation follows a structured sequence:

**Step 1: Determine Each Parent's Gross Income**
- All income from all sources: wages, self-employment, rental, interest, gifts, inheritances, unemployment, workers' comp, disability, etc. (MCSF §2.01(A))
- Exclude: public assistance (TANF, SSI, food stamps), child support received for other children

**Step 2: Deduct Specific Allowances (MCSF §2.05)**
- Federal, state, local income taxes (using actual or estimated withholding)
- Social Security/FICA taxes
- Mandatory union dues
- Mandatory retirement contributions
- Health insurance premiums for parents only (not child)
- Support paid for other natural/adopted children per prior support orders
- Reasonable business expenses for self-employed parents

→ Result: **Net Income** for each parent

**Step 3: Calculate Combined Net Income**
- Add both parents' net incomes

**Step 4: Determine Overnight Percentage**
- Count overnight parenting time for the non-custodial parent
- Threshold: ≥ 128 overnights/year triggers the shared economic responsibility calculation (MCSF §3.04)

**Step 5: Calculate Base Support**
Using the MCSF income-sharing tables (Appendix):
- At <128 overnights: straight percentage of combined income allocated to obligor
- At ≥128 overnights: offset calculation comparing what each parent would owe if the other was the custodial parent

**Step 6: Add Medical Support**
- Child's health insurance premium (MCL 552.519; MCL 552.605c)
- Uninsured medical expenses: typically split proportionally to income

**Step 7: Add Child Care Support**
- Work/school-related child care costs (MCSF §3.06)
- Adjusted for federal/state tax credits

**Step 8: Confirm Minimum Order**
- Minimum support: $25/month per child (MCSF §2.06(B)(1)) even if obligor has little or no income

**Deviation Grounds (MCSF §1.04):**
Court may deviate from the formula if application would be **unjust or inappropriate** based on:
- Additional support obligations (not in prior order)
- Educational costs
- Significant income fluctuations
- Special needs of child
- Custody arrangements not captured by overnight formula
- Health care, etc.
Court **must** state deviation grounds on the record and in the order.

> *Authority:* MCL 552.519; MCL 552.605; MCSF Manual (current edition); *Ghidotti v Barber*, 459 Mich 189 (1998)

---

### Parenting Time — MCL 722.27a Atomized

**MCL 722.27a** sets out specific parenting time rights and enforcement mechanisms:

**MCL 722.27a(1):** Parenting time is the right of the child. Either parent may petition for parenting time.

**MCL 722.27a(3):** Parenting time shall be granted in frequency, duration, and type reasonably calculated to promote a strong relationship between child and parent *unless* the court determines it would endanger the child's physical, mental, or emotional health.

**MCL 722.27a(5) — Factors Court Considers:**
1. Existence of domestic violence
2. Child's age
3. Each parent's ability to be flexible and work cooperatively
4. Whether child has special needs
5. Reasonable likelihood of abuse or neglect during parenting time
6. Reasonable likelihood of parental abduction
7. Whether a parent has failed to exercise parenting time
8. Whether a parent has established a pattern of noncompliance
9. Whether parenting time interferes with school or social activities

**MCL 722.27a(7) — Parenting Time Interference Remedies:**
When a parent **willfully denies** parenting time without good cause:
1. Court shall order makeup parenting time within a reasonable time
2. Court may order civil contempt
3. Court may impose sanctions, including fines or attorney fees
4. **Repeat violation** is grounds for modification of custody (one of the strongest arguments for custody change — *Marik v Marik*, 325 Mich App 353 (2018))

**Supervised Parenting Time:**
Court may order supervision when there is credible evidence of:
- Child abuse or neglect
- Domestic violence
- Substance abuse that affects parenting
- Credible risk of abduction
Supervision is ordered through: parenting time center, professional supervisor, neutral third party, or a family member.

---

## 6. Friend of the Court (FOC)

---

### FOC Jurisdiction & Duties

The **Friend of the Court** is an arm of the circuit court's family division operating under the Friend of the Court Act (MCL 552.501 et seq.). Every county has an FOC office.

**Core Functions:**
- Investigate and make recommendations on custody, parenting time, and support
- Monitor and enforce support orders (income withholding, license suspension, contempt referrals)
- Conduct mediation between parties (MCL 552.513)
- Maintain records of support payments through the Michigan State Disbursement Unit (MiSDU)
- Investigate parenting time complaints

**Grievance Procedure (MCL 552.501(6)):**
Any party may file a written grievance with the FOC office about the performance of its duties. If unresolved, the party may petition the circuit court for review.

**Opting Out / Waiver (MCL 552.505a):**
Parties may jointly request FOC services be waived if: (1) no minor children are involved, or (2) both parties agree and the court approves. Domestic violence history may preclude waiver.

---

### MCR 3.2xx Rules

|---|---|---|
| **MCR 3.201** | Applicability | Applies to all domestic relations actions |

---

### Key SCAO FOC Forms

| Form | Title | When Used |
|---|---|---|
| **FOC 10** | Uniform Child Support Order | All new support orders; required format statewide |
| **FOC 10a** | Uniform Child Support Order Addendum | Medical support and child care provisions |
| **FOC 23** | Objection to Referee's Recommended Order | File within 21 days of referee recommendation |
| **FOC 24** | Request for Hearing on Referee Recommendation | Triggers de novo hearing before judge |
| **FOC 50** | Motion Regarding Parenting Time | Request enforcement or modification |
| **FOC 51** | Order Regarding Parenting Time | Court order after FOC 50 hearing |
| **FOC 65** | Motion Regarding Support | Modify, enforce, or explain deviation |
| **FOC 66** | Order Regarding Support | Court order after FOC 65 hearing |
| **FOC 87** | Motion Regarding Custody | Initiates custody modification proceeding |
| **FOC 88** | Order Regarding Custody | Court order on FOC 87 motion |
| **FOC 100** | Verified Statement Regarding Minor Children | Required in all domestic relations complaints |
| **CC 375** | Personal Protection Order (Domestic) | Petition form, MCL 600.2950 |
| **CC 376** | Personal Protection Order (Non-Domestic) | Petition form, MCL 600.2950a |
| **CC 380** | Motion to Modify/Terminate PPO | Respondent's challenge to ex parte PPO |

> *All SCAO forms are available at:* https://www.courts.michigan.gov/forms/

---

### FOC Support Enforcement Toolkit — Atomized

When a support obligor fails to pay, the FOC and the court have an array of enforcement tools:

**1. Income Withholding Order (IWO) — Automatic (MCL 552.604)**
- All support orders in Michigan are automatically accompanied by an IWO
- Employer must deduct support from wages and remit to Michigan State Disbursement Unit (MiSDU) within **3 business days** of payday
- IWO binds employer; employer liability for non-compliance
- Employer may not discharge employee solely because of IWO (MCL 552.613)

**2. License Suspension (MCL 552.635; MCL 257.321a)**
- FOC may initiate suspension of: driver's license, professional/occupational licenses, hunting/fishing licenses, recreational vehicle registrations
- Notice required: obligor given **20 days** to bring account current before suspension is requested from issuing agency
- Must be at least **2 months** in arrears to trigger license action [UNVERIFIED — confirm current threshold]
- Conditional reinstatement available: payment agreement + compliance

**3. Tax Refund Intercept (MCL 552.171)**
- FOC submits account to Michigan Revenue Collection (Michigan Income Tax Refund Intercept) and federal Treasury Offset Program (TOP)
- Federal TOP intercepts federal income tax refunds, federal retirement payments
- Threshold: arrears ≥ $150 (for families on public assistance) or ≥ $500 (for others)

**4. Credit Reporting (MCL 552.637)**
- FOC may report support arrears to consumer credit reporting agencies
- Helps create financial incentive for compliance

**5. Contempt of Court (MCR 3.208; MCL 552.641)**
- Show cause order issued; obligor summoned to appear
- If obligor fails to appear: bench warrant
- At hearing: court examines ability to pay; if willful non-payment found → jail (civil contempt with purge condition) or fine
- **Ability to pay** is a jurisdictional prerequisite to civil contempt (*Tkachik v Mandeville*, 487 Mich 38 (2010))
- Purge condition: pay specific amount to be released from jail

**6. Passport Denial (42 USC 652(k))**
- Federal law requires denial/revocation of U.S. passport for persons with child support arrears ≥ $2,500
- Coordinated through federal Office of Child Support Enforcement (OCSE) and State Department

**7. Financial Institution Data Match (FIDM) (MCL 552.672)**
- FOC/OCSE matches support obligors against financial institution account records
- May freeze and seize funds to satisfy arrears

**8. Lien on Property (MCL 552.641)**
- Support arrears create automatic lien on real property in the county of the case
- Must record with register of deeds to attach to property in other counties

---

### FOC Referee Procedure — Atomized (MCR 3.207)

**Step 1: Referee Hearing**
- Referee conducts hearing on referee-eligible matters: child support, parenting time, income withholding, modification of support
- Referee is not a judge; cannot make binding orders — issues a **recommended order** (MCR 3.207(A))
- Both parties may appear and present evidence
- Referee records the hearing (audio or transcript)

**Step 2: Recommended Order**
- Referee issues written recommendation within a reasonable time after hearing
- Served on all parties with notice of the right to object

**Step 3: Objection Process (MCR 3.207(D))**
- Any party may file a **written objection** within **21 days** of notification of the recommendation
- Use **FOC Form 23** (Objection to Referee's Recommended Order)
- Objection must state **specific grounds** — general objection is insufficient
- If no timely objection: recommendation becomes an **enforceable court order** (MCR 3.207(D)(1))

**Step 4: De Novo Hearing Before Judge (MCR 3.207(E))**
- If objection filed, request a de novo hearing using **FOC Form 24**
- De novo hearing is a **fresh hearing** before the circuit judge — not review of the referee's decision
- New evidence may be presented; referee's recommendation is not binding
- Judge may adopt, modify, or reject the referee's recommendation
- **Deadline:** Request de novo hearing with the objection or promptly after

**Step 5: Appeal**
- Order following de novo hearing is a final order subject to appeal as of right to the Court of Appeals within **21 days** (MCR 7.204(A)(1))

---

## 7. Judicial Disqualification & Judicial Conduct

---

### MCR 2.003 — Disqualification of Judge

**MCR 2.003** is the primary procedural rule for seeking disqualification of a judge in Michigan.

#### Grounds for Disqualification (MCR 2.003(C))

A judge **must** be disqualified if:

| Ground | Description |
|---|---|
| **(1) Personal bias or prejudice** | The judge has actual personal bias or prejudice for or against a party or attorney |
| **(2) Personal knowledge** | The judge has personal knowledge of disputed evidentiary facts |
| **(3) Former involvement** | The judge was a material witness, attorney, or party in the proceeding |
| **(4) Financial interest** | The judge has a financial interest in the subject matter of the proceeding |
| **(5) Relationship** | The judge or a family member has a relationship with a party or attorney creating a conflict |
| **(6) Impartiality reasonably questioned** | The judge's impartiality might reasonably be questioned by an objective, disinterested observer |
| **(7) Campaign statements** | The judge made an unconditional promise or commitment about an issue in the case during a campaign |

#### Procedure (MCR 2.003(D))

1. **Party files motion** with the challenged judge stating specific facts and grounds
2. **Judge rules on own motion** — may grant or deny
3. **If denied** — party files motion for review with the chief judge (or random assignment panel)
4. **Chief judge reviews** — upholds or overrules the denial
5. **Immediate appeal** — a party may seek leave to appeal to the Court of Appeals; this does not stay proceedings unless ordered

**Timing:** Motion must be filed promptly after the basis for disqualification is discovered. Delay may constitute waiver.

> *Authority:* MCR 2.003; *Cain v Dep't of Corrections*, 451 Mich 470 (1996); *In re MKK*, 286 Mich App 546 (2009)

---

### MCJC Canons

The **Michigan Code of Judicial Conduct** (MCJC) is enforced by the **Judicial Tenure Commission** (JTC). Key canons:

| Canon | Title | Core Principle |
|---|---|---|
| **Canon 1** | Upholding the Integrity and Independence of the Judiciary | A judge shall participate in establishing, maintaining, and enforcing high standards of conduct |
| **Canon 2** | Avoiding Impropriety and the Appearance of Impropriety | A judge shall respect and comply with the law and shall act at all times in a manner that promotes public confidence |
| **Canon 2A** | Impartiality | A judge shall be faithful to the law and maintain professional competence in it |
| **Canon 2B** | Non-Use of Prestige | A judge shall not allow family or other relationships to influence the judge's judicial conduct |
| **Canon 3** | Performing the Duties of the Office Impartially and Diligently | Governs hearings, disposition of matters, disqualification |
| **Canon 3A(4)** | Patient and Dignified Treatment | A judge shall be patient, dignified, and courteous to all who appear |
| **Canon 3A(6)** | Exclusion of Ex Parte Communications | A judge shall not initiate, permit, or consider ex parte communications concerning a pending proceeding |
| **Canon 3C** | Disqualification | Same grounds as MCR 2.003; judge has independent duty to recuse |
| **Canon 3D** | Remittal of Disqualification | Parties may consent to proceed despite a disqualification ground |
| **Canon 5** | Engaging in Extra-Judicial Activities | Limitations on outside employment and activities |
| **Canon 7** | Political Activity | Restrictions on judges and candidates for judicial office |

**Canon 3A(6) — Ex Parte Communications:**  
A judge must not communicate privately with a party or counsel about a pending matter without the opposing party's knowledge. Violation is grounds for JTC complaint and may require reversal.

---

### Complaint Pathway

1. **File JTC complaint** — Judicial Tenure Commission, 3034 W. Grand Blvd., Suite 8-450, Detroit, MI 48202
   - Form: JTC-1 (available at https://www.michigan.gov/jtc)
   - No filing fee; complaint is confidential during investigation
2. **JTC investigates** — may dismiss, issue caution, or file formal complaint
3. **Formal hearing** — before a JTC master; record made
4. **JTC recommendation** — transmitted to Michigan Supreme Court
5. **Michigan Supreme Court** — final order (censure, suspension, removal, or retirement)

> *Note:* A pending JTC complaint does **not** automatically disqualify the judge or stay the case. A separate MCR 2.003 motion must be filed to disqualify the judge from a specific case.

---

### Federal Judicial Disqualification — 28 USC 455

Federal judges in E.D. Mich. or W.D. Mich. are subject to disqualification under **28 USC 455**:

**28 USC 455(a) — Catch-All:**
Any justice, judge, or magistrate shall disqualify themselves in any proceeding in which their **impartiality might reasonably be questioned**.

**28 USC 455(b) — Per Se Grounds:**
| Subsection | Ground |
|---|---|
| (b)(1) | Personal bias or prejudice concerning a party or personal knowledge of disputed evidentiary facts |
| (b)(2) | Former attorney in the matter in controversy |
| (b)(3) | Former association with law firm that was associated with the matter while judge was a member |
| (b)(4) | Financial interest in the subject matter (individually or as a fiduciary) |
| (b)(5) | Party or attorney is a person within the third degree of relationship to judge |

**Procedure — Federal:**
1. File motion to recuse addressed to the assigned judge
2. Judge rules on own motion — may recuse voluntarily
3. If denied, seek a writ of mandamus in the 6th Circuit (rarely granted — extraordinary remedy)
4. Review on appeal after final judgment for abuse of discretion

**Liteky Standard:** *Liteky v United States*, 510 US 540 (1994) — judicial rulings and conduct in the same case are almost never sufficient for disqualification; bias must stem from an extrajudicial source.

---

### JTC Investigation — Stages & Timeline

| Stage | Description | Approximate Timeline |
|---|---|---|
| **Complaint filed** | JTC-1 form submitted; screened for jurisdiction | Day 1 |
| **Screening** | Staff attorney reviews; if not frivolous, assigned for investigation | Weeks 1–4 |
| **Preliminary investigation** | Request for response from judge; review of records | Weeks 4–12 |
| **Investigation complete** | Staff recommends: dismiss, caution, formal complaint | 3–9 months |
| **Formal complaint filed** | Master appointed; formal hearing scheduled | After investigation |
| **Master's hearing** | Contested evidentiary hearing; findings of fact | 1–3 months after filing |
| **JTC recommendation** | Transmitted to Michigan Supreme Court | After master's report |
| **MSC order** | Censure, suspension, removal, or retirement | Final |

**Discipline Outcomes (Mich Const 1963, art VI, § 30):**
- **Censure** — public reprimand; no suspension
- **Censure + suspension** — temporary removal from office without pay
- **Censure + removal** — permanent removal from office
- **Compulsory retirement** — if judge is permanently disabled

**Confidentiality:**
- All JTC proceedings are **confidential** until a formal complaint is filed and served on the judge
- Once formal complaint is filed, proceedings are public

---

### Disqualification in Referee Proceedings

- **Referee** is subject to the same disqualification standards as a judge: MCR 2.003 applies
- Motion for disqualification of referee must be filed with the chief judge
- Delayed disqualification after knowledge is waived

---

## 8. Due Process Checklist

---

### Constitutional Bases

| Authority | Provision | Application |
|---|---|---|
| **U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1** | "…nor shall any State deprive any person of life, liberty, or property, without due process of law" | Federal floor; applies to all state court proceedings |
| **Mich. Const. 1963, art. I, § 17** | "No person shall be…deprived of life, liberty or property, without due process of law" | Michigan counterpart; generally coextensive with federal |
| **Mich. Const. 1963, art. I, § 20** | Rights of accused | Applies in criminal and quasi-criminal proceedings |

**Parental rights are a constitutionally protected liberty interest** under both the federal and Michigan constitutions. The government may not terminate, restrict, or alter parental rights without procedural due process.

> *Authority:* *Troxel v Granville*, 530 US 57 (2000); *Stanley v Illinois*, 405 US 645 (1972); *In re Clausen*, 442 Mich 648 (1993)

---

### Mathews v. Eldridge Balancing Test

Federal and Michigan courts apply the *Mathews v Eldridge* three-factor balancing test to determine what process is due:

| Factor | Description |
|---|---|
| **(1) Private interest** | The importance of the private interest that will be affected by the official action |
| **(2) Risk of erroneous deprivation** | The risk of an erroneous deprivation of that interest through the procedures used, and the value of additional safeguards |
| **(3) Government interest** | The government's interest, including the fiscal and administrative burdens of additional procedural requirements |

> *Authority:* *Mathews v Eldridge*, 424 US 319 (1976); *Turner v Rogers*, 564 US 431 (2011) (applying *Mathews* to civil contempt in child support); *In re Rood*, 483 Mich 73 (2009)

---

### Procedural Checklist for Family Law Hearings

Use this checklist to identify and preserve due process objections:

**Before the Hearing:**
- [ ] Adequate notice of hearing provided (MCR 2.119; MCR 3.206)
- [ ] Notice includes specific issues to be decided
- [ ] Sufficient time to prepare (MCR 2.108; MCR 2.119(C))
- [ ] All evidence to be offered has been disclosed
- [ ] Opportunity to conduct discovery (MCR 2.301 et seq.)
- [ ] No ex parte communications with the court (MCJC Canon 3A(6))

**At the Hearing:**
- [ ] Party has right to be present and heard
- [ ] Party has opportunity to present evidence and witnesses
- [ ] Party has opportunity to cross-examine adverse witnesses
- [ ] Hearsay objections preserved if improper hearsay admitted
- [ ] FOC/referee report objections preserved (MCR 3.210; FOC 23/24)
- [ ] Judge has disclosed any disqualification grounds (MCR 2.003)

**The Decision:**
- [ ] Court makes findings of fact on the record or in writing
- [ ] Court addresses all required statutory factors (e.g., all 12 MCL 722.23 factors in custody)
- [ ] Court states reasons for deviation from guidelines (if applicable)
- [ ] Order is consistent with the findings

**After the Hearing:**
- [ ] Objection to referee recommendation filed within 21 days (MCR 3.207; FOC 23)
- [ ] Motion for reconsideration filed within 21 days if appropriate (MCR 2.119(F))
- [ ] Notice of appeal filed within 21 days for final orders (MCR 7.204(A)(1))
- [ ] Transcript ordered to preserve record for appeal (MCR 7.210)

> *Failure to object at the hearing generally waives the issue on appeal.* See *Walters v Nadell*, 481 Mich 377 (2008).

---

### Notice Requirements by Proceeding Type

| Proceeding | Minimum Notice | Authority | Content Required |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Contested custody hearing** | MCR 2.119(C): 7 days for non-motion; 9 days by mail | MCR 2.119; MCR 3.206 | Issues to be heard; date, time, place |
| **Show cause/contempt** | Served personally or by mail; at least 7 days before hearing | MCR 3.208; MCR 3.606 | Specific acts alleged; possible penalties including jail |
| **PPO modification/termination hearing** | Scheduled within 14 days; service required | MCR 3.703(G)(3) | Copy of PPO; motion; hearing date |
| **Ex parte order — return date** | Within 14 days of service (PPO); within reasonable time (custody EPOC) | MCR 3.703(G); MCR 3.207(B) | Issued order; return hearing date |
| **Termination of parental rights** | Personal service required (MCR 3.920(B)(1)) | MCR 3.921; MCL 712A.19b | Petition; specific grounds; date of hearing; right to counsel |
| **Preliminary hearing (child removal)** | Within 24 hours of removal or next business day | MCR 3.965(B)(1) | Notice to all parties; right to attorney |
| **Juvenile court arraignment** | Promptly after detention; usually same or next day | MCR 3.935 | Specific charges; rights; right to counsel |
| **Administrative agency contested case** | MCL 24.271: reasonable notice before hearing | MCL 24.271 | Statement of issues; legal authority; time and place |
| **Referee recommendation — objection** | Notice of recommendation served; 21 days to object | MCR 3.207(D) | Recommendation; objection deadline; right to de novo hearing |

---

### Due Process Rights at TPR Hearing

Because termination of parental rights is among the most severe state interventions, heightened procedural due process applies:

1. **Right to appointed counsel** — indigent parents are entitled to appointed counsel (MCL 712A.17c; MCR 3.915(B))
2. **Right to notice** — personal service of petition required; published service not sufficient for parents whose addresses are known
3. **Clear and convincing evidence standard** — statutory grounds must be proven at this standard (*Santosky v Kramer*, 455 US 745 (1982))
4. **Right to be present** — parent may not be excluded from the adjudicative hearing
5. **Right to present evidence and cross-examine** — full adversarial hearing required
6. **Right to appeal** — free transcript for indigent parent (*M.L.B. v S.L.J.*, 519 US 102 (1996))
7. **Best interests must be separately found** — two-step process; statutory ground + best interest finding
8. **ICWA heightened requirements** — if ICWA applies, "beyond a reasonable doubt" + active efforts required (25 USC 1912(d)–(f))

---

### Due Process Rights at Contempt Hearings

**Civil Contempt for Non-Payment of Support:**
1. Notice of the contempt hearing in writing
2. Opportunity to present evidence of inability to pay
3. Court must inquire into current ability to pay (*Turner v Rogers*, 564 US 431 (2011))
4. If self-represented and facing incarceration, court must provide alternative procedural safeguards (notice of importance of ability-to-pay; form to dispute ability to pay; opportunity to respond to statements re: employment) (*Turner v Rogers*)
5. Purge condition must be one the contemnor is actually capable of meeting

**Criminal Contempt (PPO violations and other):**
1. Full criminal due process rights: notice of charge, right to counsel, right to jury trial if potential imprisonment > 6 months (*Bloom v Illinois*, 391 US 194 (1968))
2. Beyond reasonable doubt standard
3. Right to silence
4. Government bears burden of proof

---

## 9. Michigan Caselaw — Key Authorities

> **Note:** All citations verified against official Michigan reporters. See §16 for [UNVERIFIED] labeling policy.

---

### Custody & Best Interests

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *Eldred v Ziny* | 246 Mich App 142 (2001) | Court must make specific findings on each MCL 722.23 factor; failure is reversible error |
| *Vodvarka v Grasmeyer* | 259 Mich App 499 (2003) | Defines "proper cause" and "change of circumstances" for custody modification threshold; movant bears burden |
| *Shade v Wright* | 291 Mich App 17 (2010) | Change of circumstances must be significant; minor, normal life changes do not meet threshold |
| *Pierron v Pierron* | 486 Mich 81 (2010) | Parental relocation within Michigan; balancing test; child's established custodial environment key factor |
| *Merecki v Merecki* | unpub (Mich App) | [UNVERIFIED] Best-interest factor (j) (facilitating relationship) weighs heavily against a parent who denies access |
| *Bofysil v Bofysil* | 239 Mich App 667 (2000) | Court may not delegate custody determination to child; child's preference is one factor among many |
| *Fletcher v Fletcher* | 447 Mich 871 (1994) | Supreme Court addresses standard of review for custody findings; clear error standard applied |
| *Berger v Berger* | 277 Mich App 700 (2008) | Trial court abused discretion by failing to address all best-interest factors; remanded for findings |

---

### Parenting Time

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *Rivette v Rose-Molina* | 278 Mich App 327 (2008) | Parenting time is the child's right; custodial parent cannot unilaterally condition or deny parenting time |
| *Brown v Loveman* | 260 Mich App 576 (2004) | Parenting time schedule enforcement; court has inherent authority to hold in contempt for willful violation |
| *Kaeb v Kaeb* | 309 Mich App 556 (2015) | Parenting time modification requires proper cause/change of circumstances threshold same as custody |
| *Marik v Marik* | 325 Mich App 353 (2018) | When a parent repeatedly denies parenting time, court may change custody as a remedy |

---

### Established Custodial Environment

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *Ireland v Smith* | 214 Mich App 235 (1995) | Defines established custodial environment (ECE): child looks to that environment for guidance, discipline, necessities, and parental comfort |
| *Mogle v Scriver* | 241 Mich App 192 (2000) | ECE can exist with both parents simultaneously; court must find ECE before applying modification standard |
| *Sinicropi v Mazurek* | 273 Mich App 149 (2006) | Temporary placement during proceedings does not create ECE; court must examine totality |

---

### Child Support & Contempt

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *Ghidotti v Barber* | 459 Mich 189 (1998) | Child support formula is presumptively correct; deviation requires findings on record |
| *Sparks v Sparks* | 440 Mich 141 (1992) | Michigan Supreme Court sets standards for property division in divorce; factors analogous to best interests |
| *Tkachik v Mandeville* | 487 Mich 38 (2010) | Ability to pay is a defense to contempt; court must inquire into ability before finding contempt for non-payment |

---

### PPO & Domestic Relations

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *Pickering v Pickering* | 253 Mich App 694 (2002) | PPO requires showing of reasonable cause to believe respondent will commit prohibited conduct; vague allegations insufficient |
| *Hayford v Hayford* | 279 Mich App 324 (2008) | MCL 600.2950 requires specific acts or threats; generalized fear without objective basis insufficient |
| *Kampf v Kampf* | 237 Mich App 377 (1999) | Court has jurisdiction to modify PPO upon motion; respondent entitled to hearing |

---

### Pro Se Litigants

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *Corporan v Henton* | 282 Mich App 599 (2009) | Pro se litigants are held to the same standards as licensed attorneys; courts will not excuse procedural errors |
| *In re Gosnell Estate* | unpub (Mich App) | [UNVERIFIED] Pro se status does not relieve party of obligation to cite authority and preserve error |

> **Practice Note:** While courts do not give procedural leniency to pro se parties, they must ensure pro se parties receive meaningful access to the process. *See* *Turner v Rogers*, 564 US 431 (2011).

---

### Modification of Child Support — Key Cases

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *Kosch v Kosch* | 233 Mich App 346 (1999) | Support may be modified retroactive to date of filing motion; not to date of change in circumstances |
| *Coplai v Coplai* | unpub (Mich App) | [UNVERIFIED] Voluntary income reduction does not by itself constitute change of circumstances for support modification |
| *Cielak v Cielak* | unpub (Mich App) | [UNVERIFIED] Voluntary quit from employment to return to school: income may be imputed at former earning capacity |
| *Stout v Stout* | unpub (Mich App) | [UNVERIFIED] Court must use MCSF formula; deviation requires specific findings on the record |

### Domestic Relations — Property Division

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *Sparks v Sparks* | 440 Mich 141 (1992) | Sets out factors for equitable property division: length of marriage, contributions, age, health, prior marriage, circumstances; equitable does not mean equal |
| *Reeves v Reeves* | 226 Mich App 490 (1997) | Marital estate vs. separate property distinction; separate property traced to pre-marital assets or inheritance |
| *McNamara v Horner* | 249 Mich App 177 (2002) | Fault in causing the divorce is a relevant factor in property distribution; courts retain discretion |
| *Olson v Olson* | 256 Mich App 619 (2003) | Pension and retirement accounts are marital property subject to equitable distribution; QDRO required for division |

### Custody — Custodial Environment & Modification

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *In re AP* | 283 Mich App 574 (2009) | Where ECE exists with both parents, neither parent can modify custody without clear and convincing evidence |
| *Lombardo v Lombardo* | 202 Mich App 151 (1993) | Best-interest factors (a)–(l) are not equally weighted; court must balance all factors; no single factor is dispositive |
| *Arndt v Kasem* | unpub (Mich App) | [UNVERIFIED] Factor (j) (facilitating relationship) should be given significant weight where one parent systematically excludes the other |
| *Dowd v Dowd* | unpub (Mich App) | [UNVERIFIED] Court must consider domestic violence under factor (k) even if no criminal conviction |

### Spousal Support (Alimony)

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *Loutts v Loutts* | 298 Mich App 21 (2012) | Sets out factors for spousal support: length of marriage, contributions, age, ability to pay, needs, earning capacity; spousal support not a punishment |
| *Cassidy v Cassidy* | unpub (Mich App) | [UNVERIFIED] Cohabitation with new partner does not automatically terminate spousal support unless the order so provides |
| *Moore v Moore* | unpub (Mich App) | [UNVERIFIED] Court must consider fault as one factor in spousal support; not a free-standing right to permanent support |

---

## 10. Federal Caselaw — SCOTUS & 6th Circuit

---

### Parental Rights & Due Process

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *Meyer v Nebraska* | 262 US 390 (1923) | Liberty includes right of parents to direct education of children; early recognition of parental rights as constitutional |
| *Pierce v Society of Sisters* | 268 US 510 (1925) | State may not compel exclusive public schooling; parental right to direct upbringing confirmed |
| *Stanley v Illinois* | 405 US 645 (1972) | Unwed father has due process right to hearing before children removed; parental interest is cognizable liberty interest |
| *Troxel v Granville* | 530 US 57 (2000) | Plurality: fit parents presumed to act in best interests of children; third-party visitation statutes must give deference to parental decision |
| *Lassiter v Department of Social Services* | 452 US 18 (1981) | No absolute right to appointed counsel in parental termination; case-by-case due process analysis |
| *Palmore v Sidoti* | 466 US 429 (1984) | Race of a parent's new partner may not be the basis for a custody modification; equal protection |

---

### Child Support & Contempt

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *Turner v Rogers* | 564 US 431 (2011) | Civil contempt for failure to pay child support requires inquiry into ability to pay; unrepresented payor entitled to alternative procedural safeguards; *Mathews* test applied |
| *Hicks v Feiock* | 485 US 624 (1988) | Distinguishes civil from criminal contempt; ability-to-pay is jurisdictional to civil contempt; burden shifts to alleged contemnor once prior ability shown |

---

### Termination of Parental Rights

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *Santosky v Kramer* | 455 US 745 (1982) | Due process requires clear and convincing evidence standard before state terminates parental rights |
| *M.L.B. v S.L.J.* | 519 US 102 (1996) | State may not condition appeal of termination of parental rights on payment of transcript costs; indigent parent has right to free transcript |
| *In re Gault* | 387 US 1 (1967) | Juveniles in delinquency proceedings have due process rights including notice, right to counsel, privilege against self-incrimination, and right to cross-examine |

---

### Procedural Due Process

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *Mathews v Eldridge* | 424 US 319 (1976) | Three-factor balancing test for what process is due; private interest + risk of error + government interest |
| *Cleveland Bd. of Educ. v Loudermill* | 470 US 532 (1985) | Property interest holders entitled to pre-deprivation hearing; notice and opportunity to respond |
| *Mullane v Central Hanover Bank & Trust Co.* | 339 US 306 (1950) | Notice must be reasonably calculated under all circumstances to apprise interested parties; publication inadequate when addresses known |

---

#### 6th Circuit Key Cases

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *Mann v Berrien Cnty.* | unpub (6th Cir) | [UNVERIFIED] Summary judgment for defendant reversed; triable issue on whether CPS workers violated clearly established parental rights |
| *Kottmyer v Maas* | 436 F3d 684 (6th Cir 2006) | Social worker entitled to qualified immunity when removing child if reasonable basis for belief of abuse; no clearly established violation |
| *Teets v Cuyahoga Cnty.* | unpub (6th Cir) | [UNVERIFIED] Substantive due process claim survives where parent alleges fabricated evidence in custody proceeding |

---

### Additional SCOTUS Caselaw — Family & Child Welfare

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *Parham v J.R.* | 442 US 584 (1979) | Parents generally have authority to commit minor children to mental institutions; substantial due process rights remain but not full adversarial hearing required |
| *Schall v Martin* | 467 US 253 (1984) | Preventive detention of juveniles before trial may be constitutional when serious risk of flight or harm; *In re Gault* rights distinguished |
| *Carey v Population Services Int'l* | 431 US 678 (1977) | Constitutional privacy right extends to minors' reproductive decisions; broad state restrictions on contraceptive access to minors unconstitutional |
| *Wisconsin v Yoder* | 406 US 205 (1972) | Parental right to direct religious education overrides compulsory school attendance law as applied to Amish families |
| *Zablocki v Redhail* | 434 US 374 (1978) | Right to marry is a fundamental right; state may not condition marriage on ability to pay child support for prior children |
| *Boddie v Connecticut* | 401 US 371 (1971) | Due process prohibits state from denying access to divorce proceedings solely because of inability to pay filing fees |

### Additional 6th Circuit Key Cases — Family Law

| Case | Citation | Holding / Significance |
|---|---|---|
| *Sherbrooke v City of Pelican Rapids* | unpub (6th Cir) | [UNVERIFIED] Removal of children without exigent circumstances or court order is Fourth Amendment seizure |
| *Pittman v Cuyahoga Cnty. Dep't of Children & Family Servs.* | 640 F3d 716 (6th Cir 2011) | Social worker who removes children from home without warrant absent exigency violates Fourth Amendment |
| *Brokaw v Mercer Cnty.* | 235 F3d 1000 (7th Cir 2000) | [Persuasive 7th Cir] — Malicious prosecution by social workers in child protective context may be cognizable under § 1983 |

---

## 11. Critical Deadlines & Issue Preservation

> **WARNING:** Deadlines in Michigan are generally jurisdictional. Missing a deadline may permanently forfeit the right.

---

### Appeals

| Action | Deadline | Authority |
|---|---|---|
| **Claim of appeal — final judgment** | 21 days after entry of judgment/order | MCR 7.204(A)(1) |
| **Application for leave — interlocutory order** | 21 days after entry of order | MCR 7.205(F)(3) |
| **Cross-appeal** | 21 days after service of claim of appeal | MCR 7.207(A) |
| **Application to Michigan Supreme Court** | 56 days after Court of Appeals decision | MCR 7.305(C)(2) |
| **Appeal from referee recommendation** | 21 days to file objection (FOC 23) | MCR 3.207(D) |
| **Request for de novo hearing after referee** | 21 days from notice of recommendation | MCR 3.207(D) |
| **PPO — motion to modify/terminate** | 14 days after service of ex parte PPO | MCR 3.703(G) |
| **Transcript order for appeal** | Promptly; typically within 28 days of filing claim | MCR 7.210(B) |

---

### Post-Judgment Motions

| Motion | Deadline | Authority |
|---|---|---|
| **Motion for reconsideration** | 21 days after entry of order | MCR 2.119(F)(1) |
| **Motion for new trial** | 21 days after entry of judgment | MCR 2.611(B) |
| **Motion to amend findings** | 21 days after entry of judgment | MCR 2.517(B) |
| **Motion for relief from judgment (fraud, new evidence)** | Reasonable time; typically no more than 1 year for mistake/fraud | MCR 2.612(C) |
| **Motion to show cause (parenting time/support)** | No deadline; file as contempt arises | MCR 3.208 |

---

### Issue Preservation Rules

To preserve an issue for appeal, a party **must** raise it in the trial court first. Failure to object = waiver.

| Issue Type | How to Preserve |
|---|---|
| **Evidentiary objection** | Object at the time evidence is offered; state the specific ground (MRE 103) |
| **Constitutional claim** | Raise in trial court; general objection insufficient |
| **Sufficiency of findings** | Object on the record that court has not addressed required factors |
| **Referee recommendation** | File written objection within 21 days (FOC 23/24) |
| **Disqualification** | File MCR 2.003 motion promptly upon discovering ground |
| **PPO challenge** | File motion to modify/terminate within 14 days (MCR 3.703(G)) |
| **Contempt ability-to-pay** | Assert inability to pay at the contempt hearing; present evidence |
| **Hearsay** | Specific objection identifying the statement and hearsay ground (MRE 802) |

> *Authority:* *Walters v Nadell*, 481 Mich 377 (2008) (unpreserved error reviewed for plain error only); MCR 2.517(A)(7) (duty to request findings).

**Plain Error Standard:**
Unpreserved errors are reviewed for plain error affecting substantial rights:
1. Error occurred
2. Error was plain (clear or obvious)
3. Error affected substantial rights (outcome determinative)
4. Manifest injustice requires reversal

> *Authority:* *People v Carines*, 460 Mich 750 (1999) (criminal); *Vushaj v Farm Bureau Gen Ins Co*, 284 Mich App 513 (2009) (civil).

---

### Additional Michigan Court Deadlines — Family Division

| Action | Deadline | Authority |
|---|---|---|
| **Emergency custody order — return hearing** | Within 14 days of service of EPOC | MCR 3.207(B)(3) |
| **GAL report** | As ordered by court; typically 21 days before hearing | MCR 3.916 |
| **QDRO submission after divorce judgment** | No statutory deadline, but promptly — pension benefits vest quickly | ERISA/MCL 552 |
| **Response to complaint (family division)** | 21 days after service (MCR 2.108(A)(1)); 28 days if served by mail | MCR 2.108 |
| **Response to counter-complaint** | 21 days from service of counter-complaint | MCR 2.108 |
| **FOC recommended order — final** | 21 days after notice; if no objection, becomes enforceable | MCR 3.207(D)(1) |
| **Parenting time makeup — ordered** | Court typically orders within 30 days of missed time | MCL 722.27a(7) |
| **Support modification — retroactivity** | Back to filing date of motion; not before | MCL 552.603a; *Kosch v Kosch* |
| **Child support termination** | Age 18 or graduation from high school, whichever is later (but not beyond age 19.5) | MCL 552.605b |
| **Spousal support review** | As specified in judgment; absent provision, no automatic review | MCL 552.28 |

### Michigan Court of Appeals Specific Deadlines

| Action | Deadline | Authority |
|---|---|---|
| **Claim of appeal (final order)** | 21 days after entry of order | MCR 7.204(A)(1) |
| **Application for leave (interlocutory)** | 21 days after entry of order | MCR 7.205(F)(3) |
| **Application for leave (after delayed appeal)** | Up to 12 months after order; late application discretionary | MCR 7.205(G) |
| **Appellee's response brief** | 35 days after appellant's brief | MCR 7.212(B) |
| **Appellant's reply brief** | 21 days after appellee's brief | MCR 7.212(B) |
| **Cross-appeal brief** | 35 days after appellant's brief | MCR 7.207 |
| **Motion for reconsideration** | 21 days after COA decision | MCR 7.215(I)(1) |
| **Application to MSC** | 56 days after COA decision | MCR 7.305(C)(2) |
| **Motions in COA** | By motion; respond within 7 days (emergency) or 14 days (non-emergency) | MCR 7.211(C)(7) |

### Juvenile Court Deadlines

| Action | Deadline | Authority |
|---|---|---|
| **Preliminary hearing after removal** | Within 24 hours or next business day | MCR 3.965(B)(1) |
| **Pretrial conference** | Within 21 days of petition | MCR 3.962 |
| **Adjudicative hearing** | Within 63 days of filing of petition (if child detained) | MCR 3.972 |
| **Dispositional hearing** | Within 28 days of adjudication (if child detained) | MCR 3.973 |
| **Review hearing** | Every 91 days after disposition | MCL 712A.19 |
| **Permanency planning hearing** | Within 12 months of removal or within 30 days of finding reunification not possible | MCL 712A.19a |
| **TPR petition** (required) | After 15 months of out-of-home placement in last 22 months (ASFA) | MCL 712A.19a(8); 42 USC 671(a)(15)(E) |
| **Notice to ICWA tribe** | As soon as child welfare proceeding begins | 25 USC 1912(a) |

---

## 12. PPO Defense Toolkit

---

### Types of PPOs

| Type | Statute | Who Can Petition | Basis |
|---|---|---|---|
| **Domestic Relationship PPO** | MCL 600.2950 | Spouse, former spouse, person with child in common, dating relationship, person residing/formerly residing | Assault, threatening conduct, stalking, entry into residence |
| **Non-Domestic (Stalking) PPO** | MCL 600.2950a | Any person | Stalking (MCL 750.411h); aggravated stalking (MCL 750.411i) |
| **Sexual Assault PPO** | MCL 600.2950a | Any person who was sexually assaulted | Specific to sexual assault respondents |

---

### Ex Parte PPO — Motion to Terminate

An **ex parte PPO** is issued without notice to the respondent. Upon being served, the respondent has the right to challenge it.

**Procedure:**
1. Respondent files **Motion to Modify or Terminate PPO** (CC 380) in the issuing court
2. Motion must be filed **within 14 days of service** — this is a hard deadline (MCR 3.703(G))
3. Court **must** schedule a hearing within 14 days of the motion
4. At hearing, **petitioner bears burden** to justify continuation of PPO

> *If respondent misses the 14-day deadline, the PPO becomes permanent absent exceptional circumstances.*

---

### Hearing Rights

At the PPO hearing, the respondent has the right to:
- [ ] Be present
- [ ] Present evidence
- [ ] Cross-examine the petitioner and any witnesses
- [ ] Contest the factual basis for the PPO
- [ ] Challenge the petitioner's standing (domestic relationship)

---

### Grounds to Challenge

| Ground | Argument |
|---|---|
| **No domestic relationship** | MCL 600.2950 requires a qualifying relationship; challenge petitioner's standing |
| **Insufficient factual basis** | Vague, generalized fear without specific acts; *Pickering v Pickering*, 253 Mich App 694 |
| **No reasonable cause** | Petitioner cannot show reasonable cause to believe respondent will commit prohibited act |
| **False statements** | If petitioner made material misrepresentations, move to terminate and consider perjury referral |
| **First Amendment** | Constitutionally protected speech (political, religious) cannot be prohibited by PPO |
| **Due process** | If ex parte order was issued without the statutory predicate of irreparable harm (MCR 3.703(B)) |
| **Stalking elements not met** | For non-domestic PPO: course of conduct must constitute stalking under MCL 750.411h |

---

### Violation Defense

If charged with PPO violation (criminal contempt, MCL 764.15b; or civil contempt):

| Defense | Basis |
|---|---|
| **Lack of notice/service** | PPO must be personally served to be enforceable; constructive notice insufficient for criminal contempt |
| **No willful violation** | Unintentional contact (coincidental meeting) is not a willful violation |
| **Petitioner initiated contact** | Petitioner's own contact with respondent does not waive PPO but is relevant to scienter |
| **Modification pending** | Note: pending motion to modify does not stay the PPO |
| **Ambiguous order** | PPO language too vague to give fair notice of prohibited conduct |
| **Inability to pay (civil contempt)** | *Turner v Rogers*, 564 US 431; *Tkachik v Mandeville*, 487 Mich 38 |

> *Authority:* MCR 3.707; MCL 764.15b; *People v Pickering*, 2011 WL XXXXXX (Mich App) [UNVERIFIED]

---

### MCL 600.2950 — Prohibited Acts (Domestic Relationship PPO)

A domestic relationship PPO may prohibit any of the following acts (MCL 600.2950(1)):

| Act | Description |
|---|---|
| **(a)** | Entering onto premises |
| **(b)** | Assaulting, attacking, beating, molesting, or wounding the petitioner |
| **(c)** | Threatening to kill or physically injure the petitioner or another person |
| **(d)** | Removing minor children from the person having legal custody, except as authorized by existing custody order |
| **(e)** | Stalking as defined in MCL 750.411h or 750.411i |
| **(f)** | Purchasing or possessing a firearm |
| **(g)** | Interfering with petitioner at petitioner's place of employment or education; interfering with petitioner's employment or educational relationships or environment |
| **(h)** | Having access to information in the records of the department regarding address, employer, or school of petitioner or minor children |
| **(i)** | Engaging in conduct that imposes on or interferes with personal liberty or that causes a reasonable apprehension of violence |
| **(j)** | Posting a message through the use of any medium of communication, including the internet or a computer or any electronic medium |

**Important:** The order must specify which prohibited acts apply. A blanket "all of the above" order may be challenged on specificity grounds.

---

### MCL 600.2950a — Non-Domestic PPO — Prohibited Acts

A non-domestic stalking PPO may prohibit the same acts listed in MCL 600.2950(1)(a)–(j) above and additionally:
- Following petitioner to or from work
- Appearing at petitioner's home or workplace
- Monitoring petitioner's internet or electronic communications
- Sending petitioner electronic communications or messages

---

### Stalking — MCL 750.411h — Elements Atomized

For a **non-domestic stalking PPO** under MCL 600.2950a, petitioner must show conduct constituting **stalking** (MCL 750.411h) or **aggravated stalking** (MCL 750.411i).

**Stalking — MCL 750.411h(1):**
"Stalking" means a **willful course of conduct** involving **repeated or continuing harassment** of an individual that would cause a **reasonable person** to feel terrorized, frightened, intimidated, threatened, harassed, or molested, and that actually causes the victim to feel terrorized, frightened, intimidated, threatened, harassed, or molested.

**Required Elements:**
1. **Willful** — the conduct is intentional
2. **Course of conduct** — a pattern of behavior composed of 2 or more separate noncontinuous acts evidencing a continuity of purpose
3. **Repeated or continuing harassment** — the conduct must be more than an isolated act
4. **Objectively reasonable person** would feel terrorized, frightened, intimidated, threatened, harassed, or molested
5. **Subjectively** — the petitioner actually feels terrorized, frightened, intimidated, threatened, harassed, or molested

**Harassment — MCL 750.411h(1)(c):**
"Harassment" means conduct directed toward a victim that includes, but is not limited to, **repeated or continuing** unconsented contact that would cause a reasonable individual to suffer emotional distress.

**Aggravated Stalking — MCL 750.411i:**
Adds one or more aggravating circumstances:
- Violation of a PPO or restraining order
- Making a credible threat (express or implicit)
- Prior stalking conviction
- Victim is under 18
- Defendant was armed with a dangerous weapon

---

### PPO Penalty Schedule

| Violation | Type | Maximum Penalty |
|---|---|---|
| **Criminal contempt — PPO violation** | Criminal misdemeanor (MCL 764.15b) | 93 days jail; $500 fine (first offense) |
| **Second or subsequent PPO violation** | Criminal misdemeanor | 1 year jail; $1,000 fine |
| **Aggravated stalking** | Felony (MCL 750.411i) | 5 years; $10,000 fine |
| **Stalking — subsequent conviction** | Felony | 5 years; $10,000 fine |
| **Violation of PPO by registered sex offender** | Enhanced penalty | [UNVERIFIED — confirm current penalty] |
| **Civil contempt** | Court discretion | Fine; imprisonment until compliance (purge) |

---

## 13. Benchbooks & Citation Format

---

### Michigan Citation Format

Michigan uses the **Uniform System of Citation** with local modifications. The authoritative guide is the **Michigan Uniform System of Citation** published by the Michigan Supreme Court and updated periodically.

#### Cases

| Court | Format | Example |
|---|---|---|
| Michigan Supreme Court | *Party v Party*, [vol] Mich [page] ([year]) | *Fletcher v Fletcher*, 447 Mich 871 (1994) |
| Michigan Court of Appeals (published) | *Party v Party*, [vol] Mich App [page] ([year]) | *Vodvarka v Grasmeyer*, 259 Mich App 499 (2003) |
| Michigan Court of Appeals (unpublished) | *Party v Party*, unpublished per curiam opinion of the Court of Appeals, issued [date] (Docket No. XXXXXX) | — |
| U.S. Supreme Court | *Party v Party*, [vol] US [page] ([year]) | *Troxel v Granville*, 530 US 57 (2000) |
| 6th Circuit | *Party v Party*, [vol] F3d [page] (6th Cir [year]) | *Kottmyer v Maas*, 436 F3d 684 (6th Cir 2006) |

> **Unpublished opinions** of the Michigan Court of Appeals are not precedentially binding under MCR 7.215(C)(1) but may be cited for persuasive value with the notation "unpub op."

#### Statutes & Rules

| Authority | Format | Example |
|---|---|---|
| Michigan Compiled Laws | MCL [chapter].[section] | MCL 722.23 |
| Michigan Court Rules | MCR [chapter].[rule] | MCR 2.003(C)(6) |
| Michigan Rules of Evidence | MRE [rule number] | MRE 803(3) |
| Michigan Constitution | Mich Const 1963, art [X], § [Y] | Mich Const 1963, art I, § 17 |
| U.S. Constitution | US Const, amend [X] | US Const, amend XIV |

---

### Benchbooks & Official Publications

| Publication | Description | Where to Find |
|---|---|---|
| **Michigan Judicial Institute (MJI) Benchbooks** | Official benchbooks for circuit judges, family law, criminal, probate, and civil proceedings | https://mjieducation.mi.gov/benchbooks |
| **MJI Family Division Benchbook** | Custody, support, parenting time, PPOs, FOC | https://mjieducation.mi.gov/benchbooks |
| **MJI Criminal Proceedings Benchbook** | Criminal procedure from arraignment through sentencing | https://mjieducation.mi.gov/benchbooks |
| **SCAO Family Court Forms Manual** | All standard FOC and domestic relations forms | https://www.courts.michigan.gov/forms/ |
| **Michigan Child Support Formula Manual** | Current MCSF, updated periodically by MSC | https://courts.michigan.gov/Administration/SCAO/Resources/Documents/Publications/Manuals/foc/mcsf.pdf |
| **Michigan Uniform System of Citation** | Official citation guide | https://courts.michigan.gov/Courts/MichiganSupremeCourt/Clerks/Pages/StyleManual.aspx |
| **Michigan Rules of Court — State** | Official bound rules (Thomson Reuters / LexisNexis) | Law libraries; LexisNexis; Westlaw |
| **Attorney General Opinions** | Formal opinions of the Michigan AG interpreting state law | https://www.michigan.gov/ag/divisions/opinions |

---

### Michigan Citation Format — Advanced Rules

**Pinpoint Citations:**
- Add specific page: *Fletcher v Fletcher*, 447 Mich 871, 877 (1994)
- Add specific subsection of statute: MCL 722.23(j)
- Add specific subsection of rule: MCR 7.204(A)(1)(a)

**Michigan Register:**
- Administrative rules: Mich Admin Code R 325.xxx — cite to current Michigan Administrative Code (MAC)
- Proposed rules: Michigan Register (Mich Reg), e.g., 2024 MR 10, p 23

**SCAO Memoranda:**
- Not binding authority but persuasive; cite as: SCAO Memorandum, dated [date]

**Attorney General Opinions:**
- Formal OAG: OAG 1996, No 6896, p 1 (Feb 5, 1996)
- Informal: Unpublished opinion of the Michigan Attorney General, dated [date]

**Unpublished Court of Appeals Opinions — Caution:**
- Under MCR 7.215(C)(1): unpublished opinions are NOT precedentially binding
- May be cited for persuasive value with notation "unpub op"
- Must include: full docket number and date of issuance
- Citing published opinion in same area is always preferred

**Short-form Citations:**
- After first full citation: use case name alone or *Id.* for immediately preceding citation
- *Id. at 500* — same case, different page
- *Supra* — not used in Michigan courts (use full cite again or shortened case name)

**Court Rules — Amended:**
- When a rule has been amended, specify effective date if relevant: MCR 7.212(B) (as amended eff Jan 1, 2023)

---

## 15. Case Number Anatomy & Additional SCAO Codes

### Michigan Case Number Format

```
YY-NNNNNN-XX
```

| Component | Description | Example |
|---|---|---|
| **YY** | Two-digit year the case was filed | `24` (2024) |
| **NNNNNN** | Sequential case number within the court | `001234` |
| **XX** | Case type code (two alpha characters) | `DM` (divorce with minor children) |

*Example:* `24-001234-DM` = 2024 divorce with minor children, case 1234
